<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Gun for an individual</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the projectile weapon. <p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p>A <b>firearm</b> is any type of <a href="/wiki/Gun" title="Gun">gun</a> designed to be readily carried and used by an individual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cole_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cole-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merriam-webster.com_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merriam-webster.com-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Firearm_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Firearm-3">[3]</a></sup> The term is legally defined further in different countries (see <a href="#Legal_definitions">Legal definitions</a>).
</p><p>The first firearms originated in 10th-century <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_China" title="History of science and technology in China">China</a>, when <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">bamboo</a> tubes containing <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lead_shot" title="Lead shot">pellet</a> projectiles were mounted on spears to make the portable <a href="/wiki/Fire_lance" title="Fire lance">fire lance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Helaine_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Helaine-4">[4]</a></sup> operable by a single person, which was later used effectively as a shock weapon in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_De%27an" title="Siege of De'an">Siege of De'an</a> in 1132. In the 13th century, fire lance barrels were replaced with metal tubes and transformed into the metal-barreled <a href="/wiki/Hand_cannon" title="Hand cannon">hand cannon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAndrade201652_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAndrade201652-5">[5]</a></sup> The technology gradually spread throughout <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> during the 14th century. Older firearms typically used <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">black powder</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Propellant" title="Propellant">propellant</a>, but modern firearms use <a href="/wiki/Smokeless_powder" title="Smokeless powder">smokeless powder</a> or other propellants. Most modern firearms (with the notable exception of <a href="/wiki/Smoothbore" title="Smoothbore">smoothbore</a> <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">shotguns</a>) have <a href="/wiki/Rifling" title="Rifling">rifled</a> barrels to impart spin to the <a href="/wiki/Projectile" title="Projectile">projectile</a> for improved flight stability.
</p><p>Modern firearms can be described by their <a href="/wiki/Caliber" title="Caliber">caliber</a> (i.e. bore diameter). For pistols and rifles this is given in millimeters or inches (e.g. 7.62mm or .308 in.), or in the case of shotguns by their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauge_(bore_diameter)" title="Gauge (bore diameter)">gauge</a> (e.g. 12 ga. and 20 ga.). They are also described by the type of action employed (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Muzzleloader" title="Muzzleloader">muzzleloader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breechloader" title="Breechloader">breechloader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lever_action" title="Lever action">lever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolt_action" title="Bolt action">bolt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pump_action" title="Pump action">pump</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revolver" title="Revolver">revolver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_firearm" title="Semi-automatic firearm">semi-automatic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automatic_firearm" title="Automatic firearm">fully automatic</a>, etc.), together with the usual means of deportment (i.e. hand-held or mechanical mounting). Further classification may make reference to the type of <a href="/wiki/Gun_barrel" title="Gun barrel">barrel</a> used (i.e. <a href="/wiki/Rifling" title="Rifling">rifled</a>) and to the barrel length (e.g. 24 inches), to the firing mechanism (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Matchlock" title="Matchlock">matchlock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheellock" title="Wheellock">wheellock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flintlock" title="Flintlock">flintlock</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Percussion_lock" title="Percussion lock">percussion lock</a>), to the design's primary intended use (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a> rifle), or to the commonly accepted name for a particular variation (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Gatling_gun" title="Gatling gun">Gatling gun</a>).
</p><p>Shooters aim firearms at their targets with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hand-eye_coordination" title="Hand-eye coordination">hand-eye coordination</a>, using either <a href="/wiki/Iron_sights" title="Iron sights">iron sights</a> or <a href="/wiki/Telescopic_sight" title="Telescopic sight">optical sights</a>. The accurate range of <a href="/wiki/Pistol" title="Pistol">pistols</a> generally does not exceed 100 metres (110 yd; 330 ft), while most <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a> are accurate to 500 metres (550 yd; 1,600 ft) using iron sights, or to longer ranges whilst using optical sights. (Firearm rounds may be dangerous or lethal well beyond their accurate range; the minimum distance for safety is much greater than the specified range for accuracy). Purpose-built <a href="/wiki/Sniper_rifle" title="Sniper rifle">sniper rifles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-materiel_rifle" title="Anti-materiel rifle">anti-materiel rifles</a> are accurate to ranges of more than 2,000 metres (2,200 yd).
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-4"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Configuration"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Configuration</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-3"><a href="#Handguns"><span class="tocnumber">1.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Handguns</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more detailed list of common firearms, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_firearms" title="List of firearms">List of firearms</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_most-produced_firearms" title="List of most-produced firearms">List of most-produced firearms</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Small_Arms_and_Light_Weapons" title="Small Arms and Light Weapons">Small Arms and Light Weapons</a>.</div>
<p>A firearm is a <a href="/wiki/Gun_barrel" title="Gun barrel">barreled</a> <a href="/wiki/Ranged_weapon" title="Ranged weapon">ranged weapon</a> that inflicts damage on targets by launching one or more <a href="/wiki/Projectile" title="Projectile">projectiles</a> driven by rapidly expanding high-pressure gas produced by <a href="/wiki/Exothermic_reaction" title="Exothermic reaction">exothermic</a> combustion (<a href="/wiki/Deflagration" title="Deflagration">deflagration</a>) of a chemical <a href="/wiki/Propellant" title="Propellant">propellant</a>, historically <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_powder" title="Black powder">black powder</a>, now <a href="/wiki/Smokeless_powder" title="Smokeless powder">smokeless powder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cole_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cole-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merriam-webster.com_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Merriam-webster.com-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Firearm_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Firearm-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the military, firearms are categorized into <i>heavy</i> and <i>light</i> weapons regarding their portability by <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a>.  Light firearms are those that can be readily carried by individual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foot_soldier" title="Foot soldier">foot soldier</a>, though they might still require more than one individual (<a href="/wiki/Crew-served_weapon" title="Crew-served weapon">crew-served</a>) to achieve optimal operational capacity.  Heavy firearms are those that are too large and heavy to be transported on foot, or too unstable against <a href="/wiki/Recoil" title="Recoil">recoil</a>, and thus require the support of a <a href="/wiki/Weapons_platform" title="Weapons platform">weapons platform</a> (e.g. a <a href="/wiki/Weapon_mount#Static_mount" title="Weapon mount">fixed mount</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gun_carriage" title="Gun carriage">wheeled carriage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_vessel" title="Water vessel">water vessel</a>) to be tactically <a href="/wiki/Mobility_(military)" title="Mobility (military)">mobile</a> or useful.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Subset" title="Subset">subset</a> of light firearms that only use <a href="/wiki/Projectile#Kinetic_projectiles" title="Projectile">kinetic projectiles</a> and are compact enough to be operated to full capacity by a single infantryman (individual-served) are also referred to as <i>small arms</i>.  Such firearms include <a href="/wiki/Handgun" title="Handgun">handguns</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Revolver" title="Revolver">revolvers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pistol" title="Pistol">pistols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Derringer" title="Derringer">derringers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Long_gun" title="Long gun">long guns</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a> (including many subtypes such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-material_rifle" title="Anti-material rifle">anti-material rifles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sniper_rifle" title="Sniper rifle">sniper rifles</a>/<a href="/wiki/Designated_marksman_rifle" title="Designated marksman rifle">designated marksman rifles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_rifle" title="Battle rifle">battle rifles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbine" title="Carbine">carbines</a>), <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">shotguns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">submachine guns</a>/<a href="/wiki/Personal_defense_weapon" title="Personal defense weapon">personal defense weapons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Squad_automatic_weapon" title="Squad automatic weapon">squad automatic weapons</a>/<a href="/wiki/Light_machine_gun" title="Light machine gun">light machine guns</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_modern_armament_manufacturers" title="List of modern armament manufacturers">arms manufacturers</a>, the top firearms manufacturers are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Browning_Arms" title="Browning Arms">Browning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Remington_Arms" title="Remington Arms">Remington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colt_Defense" title="Colt Defense">Colt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sturm,_Ruger_%26_Co." title="Sturm, Ruger &amp; Co.">Ruger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smith_%26_Wesson" title="Smith &amp; Wesson">Smith &amp; Wesson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savage_Arms" title="Savage Arms">Savage</a>, <a href="/wiki/O.F._Mossberg_%26_Sons" title="O.F. Mossberg &amp; Sons">Mossberg</a> (USA), <a href="/wiki/Heckler_%26_Koch" title="Heckler &amp; Koch">Heckler &amp; Koch</a>, <a href="/wiki/SIG_Sauer" title="SIG Sauer">SIG Sauer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Walther_GmbH" title="Carl Walther GmbH">Walther</a> (Germany), <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cesk%C3%A1_zbrojovka_Uhersk%C3%BD_Brod" title="Česká zbrojovka Uherský Brod">ČZUB</a> (Czech Republic), <a href="/wiki/Glock_Ges.m.b.H." title="Glock Ges.m.b.H.">Glock</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steyr-Mannlicher" title="Steyr-Mannlicher">Steyr-Mannlicher</a> (Austria), <a href="/wiki/FN_Herstal" title="FN Herstal">FN Herstal</a> (Belgium), <a href="/wiki/Beretta" title="Beretta">Beretta</a> (Italy), <a href="/wiki/Norinco" title="Norinco">Norinco</a> (China), <a href="/wiki/Tula_Arms_Plant" title="Tula Arms Plant">Tula Arms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalashnikov_Concern" title="Kalashnikov Concern">Kalashnikov</a> (Russia), while former top producers included <a href="/wiki/Mauser" title="Mauser">Mauser</a>, <a href="/wiki/Springfield_Armory" title="Springfield Armory">Springfield Armory</a>, and Rock Island Armory under <a href="/wiki/Armscor_(Philippines)" title="Armscor (Philippines)">Armscor (Philippines)</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Firearm&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Small_Arms_Survey" title="Small Arms Survey">Small Arms Survey</a> reported that there were over one billion firearms distributed globally, of which 857 million (about 85 percent) were in <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">civilian</a> hands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smallarmssurvey.org_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-smallarmssurvey.org-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">[8]</a></sup> U.S. civilians alone account for 393 million (about 46 percent) of the worldwide total of civilian-held firearms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">[8]</a></sup> This amounts to "120.5 firearms for every 100 residents".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-8">[8]</a></sup> The world's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_forces" title="Armed forces">armed forces</a> control about 133 million (about 13 percent) of the global total of small arms, of which over 43 percent belong to two countries: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> (30.3 million) and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (27.5 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smallarmssurvey.org_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-smallarmssurvey.org-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency" title="Law enforcement agency">Law enforcement agencies</a> control about 23 million (about 2 percent) of the global total of small arms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smallarmssurvey.org_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-smallarmssurvey.org-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Configuration">Configuration</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Handguns">Handguns</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Handgun" title="Handgun">Handgun</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Full_cock3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="642" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Full_cock3.jpg/220px-Full_cock3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Full_cock3.jpg/330px-Full_cock3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Full_cock3.jpg/440px-Full_cock3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Full_cock3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Colt_Single_Action_Army" title="Colt Single Action Army">Colt Single Action Army</a> revolver, with hammer cocked back</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2892" data-file-width="3826" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg/220px-GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg/330px-GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg/440px-GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GLOCK_17_Gen_4_Pistol_MOD_45160304.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Glock" title="Glock">Glock 17</a> semi-automatic <a href="/wiki/Pistol" title="Pistol">pistol</a></div></div></div>
<p>Handguns are guns that can be used with a single hand and are the smallest of all firearms.  However, the legal definition of a "handgun" varies between countries and regions.  For example, in South African law, a "handgun" means a pistol or revolver which can be held and discharged with one hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-act60of2000_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-act60of2000-9">[9]</a></sup> In Australia, the gun law considers a handgun as a firearm carry-able or concealable about the person; or capable of being raised and fired by one hand; or not exceeding 65 cm (26 in).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www5.austlii.edu.au_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-www5.austlii.edu.au-10">[10]</a></sup> In the United States, <a href="/wiki/Title_18_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 18 of the United States Code">Title 18</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Alcohol,_Tobacco,_Firearms_and_Explosives" title="Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives">ATF</a> considers a handgun as a firearm which has a short <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buttstock" title="Buttstock">stock</a> and is designed to be held and fired by the use of a single hand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are two common types of handguns: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolvers" title="Revolvers">revolvers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_pistol" title="Semi-automatic pistol">semi-automatic pistols</a>. Revolvers have a number of firing chambers or "charge holes" in a revolving cylinder; each chamber in the cylinder is loaded with a single <a href="/wiki/Cartridge_(firearms)" title="Cartridge (firearms)">cartridge</a> or charge. Semi-automatic pistols have a single fixed firing chamber machined into the rear of the barrel, and a magazine so they can be used to fire more than one round. Each press of the trigger fires a cartridge, using the energy of the cartridge to activate a mechanism so that the next cartridge may be fired immediately. This is opposed to "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Double-action" title="Double-action">double-action</a>" revolvers, which accomplish the same end using a mechanical action linked to the trigger pull.
</p><p>With the invention of the revolver in 1818, handguns capable of holding multiple rounds became popular. Certain designs of auto-loading pistols appeared beginning in the 1870s and had largely supplanted revolvers in military applications by the end of World War I. By the end of the 20th century, most handguns carried regularly by military, police, and civilians were semi-automatic, although revolvers were still widely used. Generally speaking, military and police forces use semi-automatic pistols due to their high magazine capacities and ability to rapidly reload by simply removing the empty magazine and inserting a loaded one. Revolvers are very common among handgun hunters because revolver cartridges are usually more powerful than similar caliber semi-automatic pistol cartridges (which are designed for <a href="/wiki/Self-defense" title="Self-defense">self-defense</a>) and the strength, simplicity, and durability of the revolver design is well-suited to outdoor use. Revolvers, especially in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/.22_LR" title=".22 LR">.22 LR</a> and 38 Special/357 Magnum, are also common <a href="/wiki/Concealed_carry_in_the_United_States" title="Concealed carry in the United States">concealed weapons</a> in jurisdictions allowing this practice because their simple mechanics make them smaller than many autoloaders while remaining reliable. Both designs are common among civilian gun owners, depending on the owner's intention (self-defense, hunting, target shooting, competitions, collecting, etc.).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Long_guns">Long guns</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Long_gun" title="Long gun">Long gun</a></div>
<p>A long gun is any firearm with a notably long barrel, typically a length of 10 to 30 inches (250 to 760 mm) (there are restrictions on minimum barrel length in many jurisdictions; maximum barrel length is usually a matter of practicality). Unlike a handgun, long guns are designed to be held and fired with both hands, while braced against either the hip or the shoulder for better stability. The receiver and trigger group is mounted into a stock made of wood, plastic, metal, or composite material, which has sections that form a foregrip, rear grip, and optionally (but typically) a shoulder mount called the <i>butt</i>. Early long arms, from the Renaissance up to the mid-19th century, were generally smoothbore firearms that fired one or more ball shot, called <a href="/wiki/Musket" title="Musket">muskets</a> or <a href="/wiki/Arquebus" title="Arquebus">arquebus</a> depending on caliber and firing mechanism.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Rifles_and_shotguns">Rifles and shotguns</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">Rifle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">Shotgun</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="136" data-file-width="639" decoding="async" height="62" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg/290px-Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg/435px-Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg/580px-Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rifle_Springfield_M1903.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Springfield_Armory" title="Springfield Armory">Springfield Armory</a> <a href="/wiki/M1903_Springfield" title="M1903 Springfield">M1903 rifle</a></div></div></div>
<p>Most modern long guns are either <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a> or <a href="/wiki/Shotgun" title="Shotgun">shotguns</a>. Both are the successors of the musket, diverging from their parent weapon in distinct ways. A rifle is so named for the spiral grooves (<a href="/wiki/Rifling" title="Rifling">riflings</a>) machined into the inner (bore) surface of its barrel, which imparts a gyroscopically-stabilizing spin to the <a href="/wiki/Bullet" title="Bullet">bullets</a> that it fires.  Shotguns are predominantly <a href="/wiki/Smoothbore" title="Smoothbore">smoothbore</a> firearms designed to fire a number of <i><a href="/wiki/Shot_(pellet)" title="Shot (pellet)">shot</a></i> in each discharge; pellet sizes commonly ranging between 2 mm #9 birdshot and 8.4 mm #00 (double-aught) buckshot.  Shotguns are also capable of firing single solid projectiles called <a href="/wiki/Shotgun_slug" title="Shotgun slug">slugs</a>, or specialty (often "<a href="/wiki/Non-lethal_weapon" title="Non-lethal weapon">less lethal</a>") rounds such as <a href="/wiki/Bean_bag_round" title="Bean bag round">bean bags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tear_gas" title="Tear gas">tear gas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Breaching_round" title="Breaching round">breaching rounds</a>.  Rifles produce a single point of impact with each firing but a long range and high accuracy; while shotguns produce a cluster of impact points with considerably less range and accuracy.  However, the larger impact area of shotguns can compensate for reduced accuracy, since <a href="/wiki/Shotgun_shell#Spread" title="Shotgun shell">shot spreads</a> during flight; consequently, in hunting, shotguns are generally used for fast-flying game birds.
</p><p>Rifles and shotguns are commonly used for hunting and often also for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_defense" title="Home defense">home defense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Security_guard" title="Security guard">security guard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement" title="Law enforcement">law enforcement</a>. Usually, large game are hunted with rifles (although shotguns can be used, particularly with slugs), while birds are hunted with shotguns. Shotguns are sometimes preferred for defending a home or business due to their wide impact area, multiple wound tracks (when using buckshot), shorter range, and reduced penetration of walls (when using lighter shot), which significantly reduces the likelihood of unintended harm, although the handgun is also common.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3-7_Shooting_Competition_(Image_2_of_4)_(12753731154).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3200" data-file-width="4800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/3-7_Shooting_Competition_%28Image_2_of_4%29_%2812753731154%29.jpg/220px-3-7_Shooting_Competition_%28Image_2_of_4%29_%2812753731154%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/3-7_Shooting_Competition_%28Image_2_of_4%29_%2812753731154%29.jpg/330px-3-7_Shooting_Competition_%28Image_2_of_4%29_%2812753731154%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/3-7_Shooting_Competition_%28Image_2_of_4%29_%2812753731154%29.jpg/440px-3-7_Shooting_Competition_%28Image_2_of_4%29_%2812753731154%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:3-7_Shooting_Competition_(Image_2_of_4)_(12753731154).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Marine" title="United States Marine">US Marine</a> firing a <a href="/wiki/Mossberg_500" title="Mossberg 500">Mossberg 500</a> shotgun</div></div></div>
<p>There are a variety of types of rifles and shotguns based on the method in which they are reloaded. Bolt-action and lever-action rifles are manually operated. Manipulation of the bolt or the lever causes the spent cartridge to be removed, the firing mechanism recocked, and a fresh cartridge inserted. These two types of action are almost exclusively used by rifles. Slide-action (commonly called 'pump-action') rifles and shotguns are manually cycled by shuttling the foregrip of the firearm back and forth. This type of action is typically used by shotguns, but several major manufacturers make rifles that use this action.
</p><p>Both rifles and shotguns also come in break-action varieties that do not have any kind of reloading mechanism at all but must be hand-loaded after each shot. Both rifles and shotguns come in single- and double-barreled varieties; however, due to the expense and difficulty of manufacturing, double-barreled rifles are rare. Double-barreled rifles are typically intended for African big-game hunts where the animals are dangerous, ranges are short, and speed is of the essence. Very large and powerful calibers are normal for these firearms.
</p><p>Rifles have been in nationally featured marksmanship events in Europe and the United States since at least the 18th century when rifles were first becoming widely available. One of the earliest purely "American" rifle-shooting competitions took place in 1775 when Daniel Morgan was recruiting sharpshooters in Virginia for the impending <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>. In some countries, rifle marksmanship is still a matter of national pride. Some specialized rifles in the larger calibers are claimed to have an accurate range of up to about 1 mile (1,600 m), although most have considerably less. In the second half of the 20th century, competitive shotgun sports became perhaps even more popular than riflery, largely due to the motion and immediate feedback in activities such as skeet, trap, and sporting clays.
</p><p>In military use, bolt-action rifles with high-power scopes are common as sniper rifles, however by the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> the traditional bolt-action and semi-automatic rifles used by infantrymen had been supplemented by select-fire designs known as <a href="/wiki/Automatic_rifle" title="Automatic rifle">automatic rifles</a>.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Carbines">Carbines</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Carbine" title="Carbine">Carbine</a></div>
<p>A carbine is a firearm similar to a rifle in form and intended usage, but generally shorter or smaller than the typical "full-size" hunting or battle rifle of a similar time period, and sometimes using a smaller or less-powerful cartridge. Carbines were and are typically used by members of the military in roles that are expected to engage in combat, but where a full-size rifle would be an impediment to the primary duties of that soldier (vehicle drivers, field commanders and support staff, airborne troops, engineers, etc.). Carbines are also common in law enforcement and among civilian owners where similar size, space, and/or power concerns may exist. Carbines, like rifles, can be single-shot, repeating-action, semi-automatic, or select-fire/fully automatic, generally depending on the time period and intended market. Common historical examples include the <a href="/wiki/Winchester_Model_1892" title="Winchester Model 1892">Winchester Model 1892</a>, Lee–Enfield "<a href="/wiki/Jungle_Carbine" title="Jungle Carbine">Jungle Carbine</a>", <a href="/wiki/SKS" title="SKS">SKS</a>, <a href="/wiki/M1_carbine" title="M1 carbine">M1 carbine</a> (no relation to the larger <a href="/wiki/M1_Garand" title="M1 Garand">M1 Garand</a>) and <a href="/wiki/M4_carbine" title="M4 carbine">M4 carbine</a> (a more compact variant of the current <a href="/wiki/M16_rifle" title="M16 rifle">M16 rifle</a>). Modern U.S. civilian carbines include compact customizations of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AR-15" title="AR-15">AR-15</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruger_Mini-14" title="Ruger Mini-14">Ruger Mini-14</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beretta_Cx4_Storm" title="Beretta Cx4 Storm">Beretta Cx4 Storm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kel-Tec_SUB-2000" title="Kel-Tec SUB-2000">Kel-Tec SUB-2000</a>, bolt-action rifles generally falling under the specifications of a <a href="/wiki/Scout_rifle" title="Scout rifle">scout rifle</a>, and aftermarket conversion kits for popular pistols including the <a href="/wiki/M1911_pistol" title="M1911 pistol">M1911</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glock" title="Glock">Glock</a> models.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Machine_guns">Machine guns</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Machine_gun" title="Machine gun">Machine gun</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MG42_Sideview.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="444" data-file-width="2126" decoding="async" height="61" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/MG42_Sideview.jpg/290px-MG42_Sideview.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/MG42_Sideview.jpg/435px-MG42_Sideview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/MG42_Sideview.jpg/580px-MG42_Sideview.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MG42_Sideview.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/MG_42" title="MG 42">MG 42</a> general-purpose machine gun with retracted <a href="/wiki/Bipod" title="Bipod">bipod</a></div></div></div>
<p>A machine gun is a fully <a href="/wiki/Automatic_firearm" title="Automatic firearm">automatic firearm</a>, most often separated from other classes of automatic weapons by the use of belt-fed ammunition (though some designs employ drum, pan or hopper magazines), generally in a rifle-inspired caliber ranging between <a href="/wiki/5.56%C3%9745mm_NATO" title="5.56×45mm NATO">5.56×45mm NATO</a> (.223 Remington) for a <a href="/wiki/Light_machine_gun" title="Light machine gun">light machine gun</a> to as large as <a href="/wiki/.50_BMG" title=".50 BMG">.50 BMG</a> or even larger for crewed or aircraft weapons. Although not widely fielded until World War I, early machine guns were being used by militaries in the second half of the 19th century. Notables in the U.S. arsenal during the 20th century included the <a href="/wiki/M2_Browning" title="M2 Browning">M2 Browning</a> .50 caliber heavy machine gun, <a href="/wiki/M1919_Browning_machine_gun" title="M1919 Browning machine gun">M1919 Browning</a> .30 caliber medium machine gun, and the <a href="/wiki/M60_machine_gun" title="M60 machine gun">M60</a> <a href="/wiki/7.62%C3%9751mm_NATO" title="7.62×51mm NATO">7.62×51mm NATO</a> general-purpose machine gun which came into use around the Vietnam War. Machine guns of this type were originally defensive firearms crewed by at least two men, mainly because of the difficulties involved in moving and placing them, their ammunition, and their tripod. In contrast, modern <a href="/wiki/Light_machine_gun" title="Light machine gun">light machine guns</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/FN_Minimi" title="FN Minimi">FN Minimi</a> are often wielded by a single infantryman. They provide a large ammunition capacity and a high rate of fire and are typically used to give suppressing fire during infantry movement. The accuracy of machine guns varies based on a wide number of factors from design to manufacturing tolerances, most of which have been improved over time. Machine guns are often mounted on vehicles or helicopters and have been used since World War I as offensive firearms in fighter aircraft and tanks (e.g. for air combat or suppressing fire for ground troop support).
</p><p>The definition of a machine gun is different in U.S. law. The <a href="/wiki/National_Firearms_Act" title="National Firearms Act">National Firearms Act</a> and <a href="/wiki/Firearm_Owners_Protection_Act" title="Firearm Owners Protection Act">Firearm Owners Protection Act</a> define a "machine gun" in the United States code <i>Title 26, Subtitle E, Chapter 53, Subchapter B, Part 1, § 5845</i> as:
"... any firearm which shoots ... automatically more than one shot, without manual reloading, by a single function of the trigger". "Machine gun" is therefore largely synonymous with "automatic weapon" in the U.S. civilian parlance, covering all automatic firearms.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Sniper_rifles">Sniper rifles</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sniper_rifle" title="Sniper rifle">Sniper rifle</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="1171" decoding="async" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg/260px-G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg/390px-G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg/520px-G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G22_ohne_Schalldaempfer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Accuracy_International_Arctic_Warfare" title="Accuracy International Arctic Warfare">Accuracy International Arctic Warfare</a> series of sniper rifles is a standard issue in the armies of several countries, including those of Britain, Ireland, and <a href="/wiki/German_Army" title="German Army">Germany</a> (shown).</div></div></div>
<p>The definition of a sniper rifle is disputed among military, police, and civilian observers alike, however, most generally define a “sniper rifle” as a high-powered, semi-automatic/bolt action, precision rifle with an accurate range further than that of a standard rifle. These are often purpose-built for their applications. For example, a police sniper rifle may differ in specs from a military rifle. Police snipers generally do not engage targets at extreme range, but rather, a target at medium range. They may also have multiple targets within the shorter range, and thus a semi-automatic model is preferred to a bolt action. They also may be more compact than mil-spec rifles as police marksmen may need more portability. On the other hand, a military rifle is more likely to use a higher-powered cartridge to defeat body armor or medium-light cover. They are more commonly (but not a lot more) bolt-action, as they are simpler to build and maintain. Also, due to fewer moving and overall parts, they are much more reliable under adverse conditions. They may also have a more powerful scope to acquire targets further away. Overall, sniper units never became prominent until <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, when the Germans displayed their usefulness on the battlefield. Since then, they have become irrevocably embedded in warfare. Examples of sniper rifles include the <a href="/wiki/Accuracy_International_AWM" title="Accuracy International AWM">Accuracy International AWM</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sako_TRG-42" title="Sako TRG-42">Sako TRG-42</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CheyTac_M200" title="CheyTac M200">CheyTac M200</a>. Examples of specialized sniper cartridges include the <a href="/wiki/.338_Lapua_Magnum" title=".338 Lapua Magnum">.338 Lapua Magnum</a>, <a href="/wiki/.300_Winchester_Magnum" title=".300 Winchester Magnum">.300 Winchester Magnum</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/.408_CheyTac" title=".408 CheyTac">.408 CheyTac</a> rounds.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Submachine_guns">Submachine guns</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">Submachine gun</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1434" data-file-width="2303" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg/220px-Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg/330px-Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg/440px-Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skorpion_PICT0107.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Czechoslovak 7.65 mm <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">submachine gun</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%A0korpion_vz._61" title="Škorpion vz. 61">Škorpion vz. 61</a> designed in 1959</div></div></div>
<p>A submachine gun is a magazine-fed firearm, usually smaller than other automatic firearms, that fires <a href="/wiki/Pistol" title="Pistol">pistol</a>-caliber ammunition; for this reason certain submachine guns can also be referred to as <i>machine pistols</i>, especially when referring to handgun-sized designs such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C5%A0korpion_vz._61" title="Škorpion vz. 61">Škorpion vz. 61</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glock#9×19mm_Parabellum" title="Glock">Glock 18</a>. Well-known examples are the Israeli <a href="/wiki/Uzi" title="Uzi">Uzi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heckler_%26_Koch_MP5" title="Heckler &amp; Koch MP5">Heckler &amp; Koch MP5</a> which use the <a href="/wiki/9%C3%9719mm_Parabellum" title="9×19mm Parabellum">9×19mm Parabellum</a> cartridge, and the American <a href="/wiki/Thompson_submachine_gun" title="Thompson submachine gun">Thompson submachine gun</a> which fires <a href="/wiki/.45_ACP" title=".45 ACP">.45 ACP</a>. Because of their small size and limited projectile penetration compared to high-power rifle rounds, submachine guns are commonly favored by military, paramilitary and police forces for close-quarters engagements such as inside buildings, in urban areas, or in trench complexes.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1203" data-file-width="4443" decoding="async" height="81" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG/300px-Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG/450px-Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG/600px-Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Suomi_M31_Torpin_Tykit_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Suomi_KP/-31" title="Suomi KP/-31">Suomi M31</a> submachine with a 70-round drum magazine attached, 20- and 50-round box magazines</div></div></div>
<p>Submachine guns were originally about the size of carbines. Because they fire pistol ammunition, they have limited long-range use, but in close combat can be used in fully automatic in a controllable manner due to the lighter recoil of the pistol ammunition. They are also extremely inexpensive and simple to build in times of war, enabling a nation to quickly arm its military. In the latter half of the 20th century, submachine guns were being miniaturized to the point of being only slightly larger than some large handguns. The most widely used submachine gun at the end of the 20th century was the Heckler &amp; Koch MP5. The MP5 is actually designated as a "machine pistol" by Heckler &amp; Koch (MP5 stands for <i>Maschinenpistole 5</i>, or Machine Pistol 5), although some reserve this designation for even smaller submachine guns such as the MAC-10 and <a href="/wiki/Glock#9×19mm_Parabellum" title="Glock">Glock 18</a>, which are about the size and shape of pistols.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Automatic_rifles">Automatic rifles</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automatic_rifle" title="Automatic rifle">Automatic rifle</a></div>
<p>An automatic rifle is a magazine-fed firearm, wielded by a single infantryman, that is chambered for rifle cartridges and capable of automatic fire. The <a href="/wiki/M1918_Browning_Automatic_Rifle" title="M1918 Browning Automatic Rifle">M1918 Browning Automatic Rifle</a> was the first U.S. infantry weapon of this type, and was generally used for suppressive or support fire in the role now usually filled by the <a href="/wiki/Light_machine_gun" title="Light machine gun">light machine gun</a>. Other early automatic rifles include the <a href="/wiki/Fedorov_Avtomat" title="Fedorov Avtomat">Fedorov Avtomat</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Huot_Automatic_Rifle" title="Huot Automatic Rifle">Huot Automatic Rifle</a>. Later, German forces fielded the <a href="/wiki/StG_44" title="StG 44">Sturmgewehr 44</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, a light automatic rifle firing a reduced power "<a href="/wiki/Intermediate_cartridge" title="Intermediate cartridge">intermediate cartridge</a>". This design was to become the basis for the "<a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifle</a>" subclass of automatic weapons, as contrasted with "<a href="/wiki/Battle_rifle" title="Battle rifle">battle rifles</a>", which generally fire a traditional "full-power" rifle cartridge.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Assault_rifles">Assault rifles</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">Assault rifle</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="332" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg/290px-AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg/435px-AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg/580px-AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AK-47_assault_rifle.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/AK-47" title="AK-47">AK-47</a> is one of the most widely produced and used <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifles</a> in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Germany introduced the <a href="/wiki/StG_44" title="StG 44">StG 44</a>, and brought to the forefront of firearm technology what eventually became the class of firearm most widely adopted by the military, the assault rifle. An assault rifle is usually slightly smaller than a <a href="/wiki/Battle_rifle" title="Battle rifle">battle rifle</a> such as the American M14, but the chief differences defining an assault rifle are <a href="/wiki/Selective_fire" title="Selective fire">select-fire capability</a> and the use of a rifle round of lesser power, known as an <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_cartridge" title="Intermediate cartridge">intermediate cartridge</a>.
</p><p>Soviet engineer <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kalashnikov" title="Mikhail Kalashnikov">Mikhail Kalashnikov</a> quickly adapted the German concept, using a less-powerful 7.62×39mm cartridge derived from the standard 7.62×54mmR Russian battle rifle round, to produce the <a href="/wiki/AK-47" title="AK-47">AK-47</a>, which has become the world's most widely used assault rifle. Soon after World War II, the Automatic Kalashnikov AK-47 assault rifle began to be fielded by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and its allies in the Eastern Bloc, as well as by nations such as China, North Korea, and North Vietnam.
</p><p>In the United States, the assault rifle design was later in coming; the replacement for the M1 Garand of WWII was another John Garand design chambered for the new <a href="/wiki/7.62%C3%9751mm_NATO" title="7.62×51mm NATO">7.62×51mm NATO</a> cartridge; the select-fire <a href="/wiki/M14_rifle" title="M14 rifle">M14</a>, which was used by the U.S. military until the 1960s. The significant recoil of the M14, when fired in full-automatic mode, was seen as a problem as it reduced accuracy, and in the 1960s it was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Stoner" title="Eugene Stoner">Eugene Stoner</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AR-15" title="AR-15">AR-15</a>, which also marked a switch from the powerful .30 caliber cartridges used by the U.S. military up until early in the Vietnam War to the much less powerful but far lighter and light recoiling .223 caliber (5.56mm) <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_cartridge" title="Intermediate cartridge">intermediate cartridge</a>. The military later designated the AR-15 as the "<a href="/wiki/M16_rifle" title="M16 rifle">M16</a>". The civilian version of the M16 continues to be known as the AR-15 and looks exactly like the military version, although to conform to <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Alcohol,_Tobacco,_Firearms_and_Explosives" title="Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms and Explosives">ATF</a> regulations in the U.S., it lacks the mechanism that permits fully automatic fire.
</p><p>Variants of both the M16 and AK-47 are still in wide international use today, though other automatic rifle designs have since been introduced. A smaller version of the M16A2, the <a href="/wiki/M4_carbine" title="M4 carbine">M4 carbine</a>, is widely used by U.S. and NATO tank and vehicle crews, airbornes, support staff, and in other scenarios where space is limited. The <a href="/wiki/IMI_Galil" title="IMI Galil">IMI Galil</a>, an Israeli-designed weapon based on the action of the AK-47 is in use by Israel, Italy, Burma, the Philippines, Peru, and Colombia. <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Arms" title="Swiss Arms">Swiss Arms</a> of Switzerland produces the <a href="/wiki/SIG_SG_550" title="SIG SG 550">SIG SG 550</a> assault rifle used by France, Chile, and Spain among others, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steyr_Mannlicher" title="Steyr Mannlicher">Steyr Mannlicher</a> produces the <a href="/wiki/Steyr_AUG" title="Steyr AUG">AUG</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bullpup" title="Bullpup">bullpup</a> rifle in use in Austria, Australia, New Zealand, Ireland, and Saudi Arabia among other nations.
</p><p>Modern designs call for compact weapons retaining firepower. The bullpup design, by mounting the magazine behind the trigger, unifies the accuracy and firepower of the traditional assault rifle with the compact size of the submachine gun (though submachine guns are still used); examples are the French <a href="/wiki/FAMAS" title="FAMAS">FAMAS</a> and the British <a href="/wiki/SA80" title="SA80">SA80</a>.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_defense_weapons">Personal defense weapons</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Personal_defense_weapon" title="Personal defense weapon">Personal defense weapon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FN_P90_PDW.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1107" data-file-width="2415" decoding="async" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/FN_P90_PDW.jpg/220px-FN_P90_PDW.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/FN_P90_PDW.jpg/330px-FN_P90_PDW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/FN_P90_PDW.jpg/440px-FN_P90_PDW.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FN_P90_PDW.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/FN_P90" title="FN P90">FN P90</a> PDW</div></div></div>
<p>A recently developed class of firearm is the <a href="/wiki/Personal_defense_weapon" title="Personal defense weapon">personal defense weapon</a> or PDW, which is in simplest terms a <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">submachine gun</a> designed to fire ammunitions with ballistic performance similar to rifle cartridges.  While a submachine gun is desirable for its compact size and ammunition capacity, its pistol cartridges lack the penetrating capability of a rifle round.  Conversely, rifle bullets can pierce light armor and are easier to shoot accurately, but even a <a href="/wiki/Carbine" title="Carbine">carbine</a> such as the Colt M4 is larger and/or longer than a submachine gun, making it harder to maneuver in close quarters.  The solution many firearms manufacturers have presented is a weapon resembling a submachine gun in size and general configuration, but which fires a higher-powered armor-penetrating round (often specially designed for the weapon), thus combining the advantages of a carbine and submachine gun.  This also earned the PDWs an infrequently used nickname—the submachine carbines.  The <a href="/wiki/FN_P90" title="FN P90">FN P90</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heckler_%26_Koch_MP7" title="Heckler &amp; Koch MP7">Heckler &amp; Koch MP7</a> are the most famous examples of PDWs.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_rifles">Battle rifles</span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_rifle" title="Battle rifle">Battle rifle</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scar_H_Standard.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="232" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="84" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Scar_H_Standard.png/290px-Scar_H_Standard.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Scar_H_Standard.png/435px-Scar_H_Standard.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Scar_H_Standard.png/580px-Scar_H_Standard.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scar_H_Standard.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgian</a> <a href="/wiki/FN_SCAR#SCAR-H" title="FN SCAR">FN SCAR-H</a></div></div></div>
<p>Battle rifles are another subtype of rifle, usually defined as <a href="/wiki/Selective_fire" title="Selective fire">selective fire</a> rifles that use full power rifle cartridges, examples of which include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7.62x51mm_NATO" title="7.62x51mm NATO">7.62x51mm NATO</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7.92x57mm_Mauser" title="7.92x57mm Mauser">7.92x57mm Mauser</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7.62x54mmR" title="7.62x54mmR">7.62x54mmR</a>. These serve similar purposes as assault rifles, as they both are usually employed by ground infantry. However, some prefer battle rifles due to their more powerful cartridge, despite added recoil. Some semi-automatic sniper rifles are configured from battle rifles.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Function">Function</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firearm_action" title="Firearm action">Firearm action</a></div>
<p>Firearms are also categorized by their functioning cycle or "action" which describes their loading, firing, and unloading cycle.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Manual">Manual</span></h4>
<p>The earliest evolution of the firearm, there are many types of manual action firearms. These can be divided into two basic categories: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_shot" title="Single shot">single shot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Repeating_rifle" title="Repeating rifle">repeating</a>.
</p><p>A single shot firearm can only be fired once per equipped barrel before it must be reloaded or charged via an external mechanism or series of steps. A repeating firearm can be fired multiple times, but can only be fired once with each subsequent pull of the trigger or ignite. Between trigger pulls, the firearm's action must be reloaded or charged via an internal mechanism.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Lever_action">Lever action</span></h5>
<p>A gun that has a lever that is pulled down and then back up to expel the old cartridge and then load a new round.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Pump-action">Pump-action</span></h5>
<p>Pump-action weapons are primarily shotguns. Pump-action is created when the user slides a lever (usually a grip) and it brings a new round into the chamber while expelling the old one.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Bolt_action">Bolt action</span></h5>
<p>Bolt action is a type of manual firearm action that is operated by directly manipulating the bolt via a bolt handle, which is most commonly placed on the right-hand side of the weapon (as most users are right-handed).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-automatic">Semi-automatic</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_firearm" title="Semi-automatic firearm">Semi-automatic firearm</a></div>
<p>A semi-automatic, self-loading, or "auto loader" firearm is one that performs all steps necessary to prepare it for firing again after a single discharge until cartridges are no longer available in the weapon's feed device or magazine. Autoloaders fire one round with each pull of the trigger. Some people confuse the term with "fully automatic" firearms.  (See next.) While some semi-automatic rifles may resemble military-style firearms, they are not properly classified as "Assault Weapons" which refers to those that continue to fire until the trigger is no longer depressed.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Automatic">Automatic</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automatic_firearm" title="Automatic firearm">Automatic firearm</a></div>
<p>An <i>automatic</i> firearm, or "fully automatic", "fully auto", or "full auto", is generally defined as one that continues to load and fire cartridges from its magazine as long as the trigger is depressed (and until the magazine is depleted of available ammunition.) The first weapon generally considered in this category is the <a href="/wiki/Gatling_gun" title="Gatling gun">Gatling gun</a>, originally a carriage-mounted, crank-operated firearm with multiple rotating barrels that was fielded in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. The modern trigger-actuated machine gun began with various designs developed in the late 19th century and fielded in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Maxim_gun" title="Maxim gun">Maxim gun</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lewis_Gun" title="Lewis Gun">Lewis Gun</a>, and <a href="/wiki/MG_08" title="MG 08">MG 08 "Spandau"</a>. Most automatic weapons are classed as long guns (as the ammunition used is of a similar type as for rifles, and the recoil of the weapon's rapid fire is better controlled with two hands), but handgun-sized automatic weapons also exist, generally in the "submachine gun" or "machine pistol" class.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Selective_fire">Selective fire</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Selective_fire" title="Selective fire">Selective fire</a></div>
<p><b>Selective fire</b>, or "select fire", means the capability of a weapon's fire control to be adjusted in either semi-automatic, fully automatic firing modes, or 3-round bursts.  The modes are chosen by means of a selector, which varies depending on the weapon's design.  Some selective-fire weapons have <a href="/wiki/Burst_mode_(weapons)" title="Burst mode (weapons)">burst fire</a> mechanisms built in to limit the maximum number of shots fired in fully automatic mode, with the most common limits being two or three rounds per trigger pull.  The presence of selective-fire modes on firearms allows more efficient use of ammunition for specific tactical needs, either precision-aimed or <a href="/wiki/Suppressive_fire" title="Suppressive fire">suppressive fire</a>.  This capability is most commonly found on military weapons of the 20th and 21st centuries, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifles</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_as_a_blunt_weapon">Use as a blunt weapon</span></h2>
<p>Firearms can be used as <a href="/wiki/Blunt_instrument" title="Blunt instrument">blunt weapons</a>, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Close-quarters_combat" title="Close-quarters combat">Close-quarters combat</a>, or when <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">ammunition</a> for the firearm has run out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kmaga_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-kmaga-14">[14]</a></sup> It is also an effective battle strategy when ammunition supply is low since knocking out enemies without firing the gun allows the user to save as much ammunition as possible for later, more critical use.
</p><p>New recruits of the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">Israel Defense Forces</a> undergo training on the safe practice of using the <a href="/wiki/M16_rifle" title="M16 rifle">M16</a> <a href="/wiki/Assault_rifle" title="Assault rifle">assault rifle</a> as a blunt weapon, mainly so that in close-quarter fighting, the weapon cannot be pulled away from them. Other training includes the recruit learning how to jab parts of the body with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muzzle_(firearm)" title="Muzzle (firearm)">muzzle</a> and using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stock_(firearm)" title="Stock (firearm)">butt stock</a> as a weapon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kmaga_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-kmaga-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Forensic_medicine" title="Forensic medicine">Forensic medicine</a> recognizes evidence for various types of  <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blunt-force_injuries" title="Blunt-force injuries">blunt-force injuries</a> produced by firearms. For example, "pistol-whipping" typically leaves semicircular or triangular lacerations of skin produced by the butt of a pistol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>In armed robberies, beating the victims with firearms is a more common way to complete the robbery, rather than shooting or stabbing them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Examples include:
</p>
<ul><li>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Butt_stroking" title="Butt stroking">Butt stroking</a>", striking with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stock_(firearm)" title="Stock (firearm)">butt stock</a> of a firearm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pistol-whipping" title="Pistol-whipping">Pistol-whipping</a>, striking someone with a <a href="/wiki/Handgun" title="Handgun">handgun</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>Striking with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muzzle_(firearms)" title="Muzzle (firearms)">muzzle</a> end of a firearm without a <a href="/wiki/Bayonet" title="Bayonet">bayonet</a> attached.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg/220px-Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg/330px-Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg/440px-Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yuan_chinese_gun.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hand_cannon" title="Hand cannon">Hand cannon</a> from the Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yuan_Dynasty" title="Yuan Dynasty">Yuan Dynasty</a> (1271–1368)</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_firearm" title="History of the firearm">History of the firearm</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_gunpowder" title="History of gunpowder">History of gunpowder</a></div>
<p>The first primitive firearms were invented about 1250 AD in <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_China" title="History of science and technology in China">China</a> when the man-portable <a href="/wiki/Fire_lance" title="Fire lance">fire lance</a> (a bamboo or metal tube that could shoot ignited <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a>) was combined with projectiles such as scrap metal, broken porcelain, or darts/arrows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Helaine_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Helaine-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>An early depiction of a firearm is a sculpture from a cave in <a href="/wiki/Sichuan" title="Sichuan">Sichuan</a>, China. The sculpture dates to the 12th century<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and represents a figure carrying a vase-shaped <a href="/wiki/Bombard_(weapon)" title="Bombard (weapon)">bombard</a>, with flames and a <a href="/wiki/Round_shot" title="Round shot">cannonball</a> coming out of it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChase200331–32_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChase200331–32-22">[22]</a></sup> The oldest surviving gun, a <a href="/wiki/Hand_cannon" title="Hand cannon">hand cannon</a> made of bronze, has been dated to 1288 because it was discovered at a site in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Acheng_District" title="Acheng District">Acheng District</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heilongjiang" title="Heilongjiang">Heilongjiang</a>, China, where the <i>Yuan Shi</i> records that battles were fought at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-needham_volume_5_part_7_293_294_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-needham_volume_5_part_7_293_294-23">[23]</a></sup> The firearm had a 6.9 inch barrel of a 1-inch diameter, a 2.6 inch chamber for the gunpowder and a socket for the firearm's handle. It is 13.4 inches long and 7.8 pounds without the handle, which would have been made of wood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChase200332_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChase200332-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Arabs and <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a> had firearms in the late-13th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Europeans obtained firearms in the 14th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChase20031_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChase20031-28">[28]</a></sup> The Koreans adopted firearms from the Chinese in the 14th century. The Iranians (first <a href="/wiki/Aq_Qoyunlu" title="Aq Qoyunlu">Aq Qoyunlu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Safavids" title="Safavids">Safavids</a>) and Indians (first <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughals</a>) all got them no later than the 15th century, from the Ottoman Turks. The people of the <a href="/wiki/Nusantara_(archipelago)" title="Nusantara (archipelago)">Nusantara</a> archipelago of Southeast Asia used the <a href="/wiki/Java_arquebus" title="Java arquebus">long arquebus</a> at least by the last quarter of the 15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:222_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-:222-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 23">: 23 </span></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Satinggar_Malay.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="48" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Satinggar_Malay.jpg/220px-Satinggar_Malay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Satinggar_Malay.jpg/330px-Satinggar_Malay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Satinggar_Malay.jpg/440px-Satinggar_Malay.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Satinggar_Malay.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Istinggar" title="Istinggar">istinggar</a>, a result of Indo-Portuguese gun-making traditions</div></div></div>
<p>Even though the knowledge of making gunpowder-based weapons in the <a href="/wiki/Nusantara_(archipelago)" title="Nusantara (archipelago)">Nusantara</a> archipelago had been known after the failed <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Java" title="Mongol invasion of Java">Mongol invasion of Java</a> (1293), and the predecessor of firearms, the <a href="/wiki/Hand_cannon" title="Hand cannon">pole gun</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bedil_tombak" title="Bedil tombak">bedil tombak</a>), was recorded as being used by Java in 1413,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:72_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-:72-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 245">: 245 </span></sup> the knowledge of making "true" firearms came much later, after the middle of 15th century. It was brought by the <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islamic</a> nations of West Asia, most probably the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>. The precise year of introduction is unknown, but it may be safely concluded to be no earlier than 1460.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:222_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-:222-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 23">: 23 </span></sup> Before the arrival of the Portuguese in Southeast Asia, the natives already possessed firearms, the <a href="/wiki/Java_arquebus" title="Java arquebus">Java arquebus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="934" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png/220px-Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png/330px-Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png/440px-Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_eastern_matchlock_evolution.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A) The matchlock gun with button for trigger, which came to Lisbon from Bohemia, used by the Portuguese until the conquest of Goa in 1510. B) The Indo-Portuguese matchlock gun resulted from the combination of Portuguese and Goan gunmaking. C) The Japanese matchlock gun appeared as a copy of the first firearm introduced in the Japanese islands.</div></div></div>
<p>The technology of firearms in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> further improved after the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Malacca_(1511)" title="Capture of Malacca (1511)">Portuguese capture of Malacca</a> (1511).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Starting in the 1513, the traditions of German-Bohemian gun-making merged with Turkish gun-making traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 39–41">: 39–41 </span></sup> This resulted in the Indo-Portuguese tradition of matchlocks. Indian craftsmen modified the design by introducing a very short, almost pistol-like buttstock held against the cheek, not the shoulder, when aiming. They also reduced the caliber and made the gun lighter and more balanced. This was a hit with the Portuguese who did a lot of fighting aboard ship and on river craft, and valued a more compact gun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 41">: 41 </span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">Malaccan</a> gunfounders,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Template:Typo_help_inline" title="Template:Typo help inline"><span title="Expert help is needed to correct the spelling of this word or mark it as OK. (April 2020)">check spelling</span></a></i>]</sup> compared as being in the same level with those of Germany, quickly adapted these new firearms, and thus a new type of arquebus, the <a href="/wiki/Istinggar" title="Istinggar">istinggar</a>, appeared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 385">: 385 </span></sup> The Japanese did not acquire firearms until the 16th century, and then from the Portuguese rather than from the Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChase200331–32_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChase200331–32-22">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1992" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg/170px-Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg/255px-Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg/340px-Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jacob_de_Gheyn_-_Wapenhandelinge_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Musketeer" title="Musketeer">musketeer</a> (1608)</div></div></div>
<p>Developments in firearms accelerated during the 19th and 20th centuries. Breech-loading became more or less a universal standard for the reloading of most hand-held firearms and continues to be so with some notable exceptions (such as mortars). Instead of loading individual rounds into weapons, magazines holding multiple munitions were adopted—these aided rapid reloading. Automatic and semi-automatic firing mechanisms meant that a single soldier could fire many more rounds in a minute than a vintage weapon could fire over the course of a battle. Polymers and alloys in firearm construction made weaponry progressively lighter and thus easier to deploy. Ammunition changed over the centuries from simple metallic ball-shaped projectiles that rattled down the barrel to bullets and cartridges manufactured to high precision. Especially in the past century<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Relative_time_references" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="Clarify the applicable timeframe so that it is unambiguous when read at a later date. (February 2022)">timeframe?</span></a></i>]</sup> particular attention has focused on accuracy and sighting to make firearms altogether far more accurate than ever before. More than any single factor though, firearms have proliferated due to the advent of mass production—enabling arms-manufacturers to produce large quantities of weaponry to a consistent standard.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Velocities of bullets increased with the use of a "jacket" of metals such as copper or copper alloys that covered a lead core and allowed the bullet to glide down the barrel more easily than exposed lead. Such bullets are designated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (February 2022)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> as "full metal jacket" (FMJ). Such FMJ bullets are less likely to fragment on impact and are more likely to traverse through a target while imparting less energy. Hence, FMJ bullets impart less tissue damage than non-jacketed bullets that expand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> This led to their adoption for military use by countries adhering to the <a href="/wiki/Hague_Conventions_of_1899_and_1907" title="Hague Conventions of 1899 and 1907">Hague Convention of 1899</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>That said, the basic principle behind firearm operation remains unchanged to this day.
